Jamison Brereton

67 (508)
Mitra and Varun╠гa
Bharadv─Бja B─Бrhaspatya
11 verses: triс╣гс╣нubh
This is the only hymn dedicated to Mitra and Varuс╣Зa in Maс╣Зс╕Нala VI, though Indra and Varuс╣Зa are the recipients of the next, unremarkable hymn. By contrast, this hymn is obscure in reference and meaning, and full of rare words, unclear morpho logical forms, contorted phraseology, puzzling imagery, and ellipses difficult to fill. Our interpretation of the hymn both in detail and in general outline differs from the many incompatible interpretations offered by other scholars (differences that we cannot discuss here), but our interpretation does produce a clear structure within which the many puzzles can be evaluated.
The hymn begins straightforwardly enough, with an exhortation to the priests to offer ritual praise to Mitra and Varuс╣Зa (vs. 1) and an invitation to the two gods to come to our ritual sacrifice (vss. 2, 3ab). This first section ends (3cd), in our view, with an elaborated version of 1ab, declaring the godsтАЩ power to control even the rich and powerful.
The ritual context returns later in the hymn (vss. 7тАУ8), and the two ritually oriented portions frame a section relating to the birth of Mitra and Varuс╣Зa from Aditi (vs. 4) and the powers they assumed to regulate the cosmos (vss. 5тАУ6). The allusion to their birth recalls the lengthy birth narrative of the Maruts in the immediately preceding hymn (VI.66.1тАУ5). With the return to the ritual situation, the two gods are first exhorted to drink the soma, whose preparation is described in enigmatic terms (vs. 7). In verse 8, again in our view, the two gods receive a summons from Agni (not named), the ritual fire through whom they will con sume ghee, because he finds they are not there. (See the calls in the structurally matching vss. 2тАУ3.)
This absence leads to the final section of the hymn (vss. 9тАУ11), which appears to treat the rivalry among competing sacrificers. If Mitra and Varuс╣Зa are not at our sacrifice (vs. 8b), they must be elsewhere. The poet describes these competi tors in extremely negative terms (vs. 9) as violating the ordinances that are the most prominent feature of Mitra and Varuс╣ЗaтАЩs moral command. In contrast, verse 10 presents the proper ritual behavior and attitudes of our side, ending with yet another affirmation of the godsтАЩ power to control and set in place the people (10d, reminiscent of 1cd and 3cd). And in the final verse (11) we are ourselves properly placed in the shelter of Mitra and Varuс╣Зa (a placement first requested in vs. 2), hoping for generous gifts when the soma sacrifice is performed. The last half-verse refers, in our view, to this sacrifice: the cows are the milk mixture pursuing the straight-flying soma; the bold bull in battle-lust is also the soma. But the expressions also evoke martial images appropriate to the rivalry among sacrificers found in the preceding two verses. It is worth not
ing that the preceding hymn also made brief allusion to sacrificial rivalry in its final verse (VI.66.11).

Jamison Brereton Notes

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬ(I proceed) by my praises to exalt you, Mira and Varuс╣Зa, the eldest of all existing things; you two, though not the same, are the irmest resrainers with your arms, and hold men back (from eil) as they check (horses) with reins.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Of all beings the most preeminent, Mitra and Varuс╣Зa are to be
continuously strengthened by your songs.
The best controllers, the two without equal, who, like reins, firmly
control the peoples with their own arms.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The hymn does not start promisingly, with a bad, and unfixable, cadence in p─Бda a (jyс║╜╠Бс╣гс╣нhatam─Б). P─Бda c also ends with a superlative (y├бmiс╣гс╣нh─Б), which makes a fine cadence. Perhaps this morphological parallelism invited the deployment of the double splv. jyс║╜с╣гс╣нhatam─Б in this unfavorable position.

Both Geldner and Renou predicate the infin. v─Бvс╣Ыdh├бdhyai to a supplied 1st pl. (e.g., тАЬM+V тАж wollen wir erbauen тАжтАЭ), but there is no reason why the dual dvandva mitr─Б╠Бv├бruс╣З─Б canтАЩt be a nom., with a passive reading of the infin., as I take it. In RenouтАЩs case the supposed 1st ps. subj. leads him to take vaс╕е as obj. (тАЬvous les plus puissants тАжтАЭ), though of course it is plural and does not match the referents in number and, compounding the grammatical lapses, to tr. mitr─Б╠Бv├бruс╣З─Б as voc. (тАЬ├┤ Varuс╣Зa-MitraтАЭ).

This was not RenouтАЩs finest hour. Geldner manages to shift vaс╕е off into an oblique role (тАЬf├╝r euch,тАЭ presumably referring to the human beneficiaries of the 1st ps. poet-ritualistsтАЩ activities), but absent a 1st ps. subj., vaс╕е can be attached directly to the poetsтАЩ songs used for strengthening, as in the published translation

In c the grammatical identity of ra┼Ыm─Б╠Б(in sandhi with the simile particle ra┼Ыm├йva) is unclear. It is generally taken, I think correctly, to the -n-stem ra┼Ыm├бn-, otherwise found only in cmpds. Grassmann calls it an instr., and Wackernagel concurs (AiG III.268), as does Renou (clearer in the comm. [EVP VII] than in the weaselly tr. тАЬcomme (avec) une r├кneтАЭ [EVP V]). But -m─Б instr. to -man-stems are rare; AiG cites only the likewise hapax dr─Бghm─Б╠Бin X.70.4. We might rather expect *ra┼Ы(a)n─Б╠Бor the like (cf. mahin─Б╠Бto mahim├бn-), and in fact such a posited form might yield the well-attested - ─Б-stem ra┼Ыan─Б╠Б- тАШhalterтАЩ as a decasuative from the instr. (though the Iranian forms showing this same internal vowel [see EWA s.v.] might give us pause). Geldner by contrast takes it as a nom. sg., which is grammatically impeccable as long as the stem is masc. (Since its other two occurences are in bahuvr─лhis, it is impossible to be sure, but suffix-accented -m├бn-stems are in fact generally masc.; cf. AiG II.2.754.) Either nom. or instr. would work fine in the passage; in the former case the comparison would be to Mitra and Varuс╣Зa as controllers; in the latter to the arms with which they perform the controlling (b─Бh├║bhiс╕е sva├нс╕е). In neither case would ra┼Ыm─Б╠Бmatch the frame in number. I have followed Geldner in taking it as a nom., though I would like it to be dual, like ap├бs─Б in 3c, but this is morphologically impossible.

The verb form yam├бtuс╕е is generally assigned to the pf. stem (Grassmann, Wh Rts, K├╝mmel), though Lubotsky lists it with the root aor., labelling it a nonce. K├╝mmel (399) derives this nonredupl. pf. by analogy to тАЬnur scheinbar reduplikationslosem takс╣гathur : takс╣гurтАЭ to the 3rd pl. injunc. root aor. yamur. Since there is no real semantic connection between the two roots тИЪyam and тИЪtakс╣г, and the supposed model takс╣гathur is found only once in the RV, in Maс╣Зс╕Нala X (as opposed to the well-established redupl. pf. tat├бkс╣гa, etc.), this seems an unlikely channel. A more likely one is found in the immediate context: the p─Бda ends тАж yam├бtur y├бmiс╣гс╣нh─Б, with the dual splv. тАЬbest controllersтАЭ serving as subj. to the etymologically identical verb. In these circumstances substituting the root syllable yam found in the splv. for the weak form yem found in the proper dual pf. yem├бthur (2x; cf. also 3rd du. yematur) would not be surprising.

Griffith

NOW Mitra-Varuna shall be exalted high by your songs, noblest of all existing;
They who, as ’twere with reins are best Controllers, unequalled with their arms to check the people.

рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрд╛ рдЬреЛрд╢реА тЖР рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рдо) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThis my praise is addressed to you both, and proceeds to you beloved (deities) together with the oblation; the sacred grass is spread before you; grant us, Mitra and Varuс╣Зa an unassailable dwelling, that through your favour, munificent divinities, may be a (secure) shelter.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

This inspired thought from me is spread forth for you two, (calling you) two dear ones with homage to the ritual grass.
Hold forth to us, Mitra and Varuс╣Зa, the unbesiegable shelter of yours that provides defense, o you of good drops.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The first hemistich displays a sort of contrastive ritual synesthesia. In the first p─Бda an inspired thought (man─лс╣г─Б╠Б) is тАШspread forthтАЩ (pr├б stс╣Ыс╣З─лte), an action not literally applicable to a verbal product but suitable to the barhis or ritual grass found in b, which is not the obj. of this verb. What is going on in b is not clear until we reach the next vs. The b p─Бda of 2 contains a set of apparently unconnected notions without a unifying verb: ├║pa priy─Б╠Бn├бmas─Б barh├нr ├бcha тАЬup to, the two dear ones (or, with a dear one), with homage, to the ritual grass,тАЭ but the corresponding p─Бda in 3 pulls together this disarray: ├║pa priy─Б╠Бn├бmas─Б h┼лy├бm─Бn─Б. The missing verbal action is тАШcallтАЩ, and now the two dear ones, the instrumental homage, and the barhis all make sense. I therefore (with Geldner, but not Renou) supply a form of тАШcallтАЩ in 2b. And тАШcallтАЩ is more appropriate to the inspired thought of p─Бda a than the spreading that occurred there. In the published translation I supply a participial form modifying the inspired thought and having active semantics, with priy─Б╠Бas acc. obj. (тАЬcalling [you] two dear onesтАЭ). I now see that it might be desirable to supply the exact form found in the next vs., the dual pass. h┼лy├бm─Бn─Б, tr. тАЬтАж you two, the dear ones being called тАжтАЭ However, there is a grammatical obstacle, in that v─Бm in 2a must be a gen./dat. enclitic, not an acc., and therefore there is no available acc. in the structural frame of the hemistich that a passive participle could modify. This might be finessed by taking b as a sort of loosely connected new start. However, I prefer to stay with the published translation, both for the syntactic reasons just mentioned, and because it makes the connection between the inspired thought and the call to the gods more direct.

The nominal rel. cl. y├бd v─Бс╣Г var┼лthy├аm is another ex. of an izafe-like construction. Here, since nothing follows it but a voc., it does not appear embedded, as many such phrases do, but it adds to the dossier of these constructions.

Griffith

To you Two Gods is this my thought extended, turned to the sacred grass with loving homage.
Give us, O Mitra-Varuna, a dwelling safe from attack, which ye shall guard, Boon-Givers!

Geldner

Dies Gedicht wird euch von mir als Teppich hingebreitet; ich rufe die Beliebten unter Verneigung zum Barhis her. Gew├дhret uns, Mitra und Varuna, euren unangreifbaren, schirmenden Schutz, den ihr Gabensch├╢nen habt!

Grassmann

Dies Andachtslied ward euch von mir gestreuet, hin auf den Streusitz demuthsvoll, ihr lieben; Reicht sichern Schutz uns, Varuna und Mitra, den ihr gew├дhrt, der schirmt, o gabenreiche.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬCome, Mitra and Varuс╣Зa, beloved by all, and invoked with reveence to the propitious ite, you who by your bounty support men labouring for sustenance as a work man (maintains himself) by work.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Drive hither, Mitra and Varuс╣Зa, dear ones being called to (the ritual grass) with good recitation, with homage.
You two who like industrious workers firmly (control) (even) the peoples ensconced in prosperity, you set in their place even those (who
themselves say) тАЬlisten!тАЭ [=bosses], with your greatness.

Jamison Brereton Notes

For the connection of the first hemistich, and esp. b, with 2ab, esp. b, see comm. on the preceding vs. Here, since Mitra and Varuс╣Зa are subjects, the pass.

participle h┼лy├бm─Бn─Б is in the nom. The 2nd hemistich is extremely problematic. Among other things, the rel. prn.

ya├║ in c calls for an accented verb, but the only finite verb in the hemistich is unaccented yatathaс╕е in d; the hapax apnasth├бс╕е in c is of unclear meaning and has an uncertain grammatical identity; the following simile ap├бseva has been variously interpr.; ┼Ыrudh─лyat├бс╕е is a hapax denominative part.; and even if all these questions are solved, what does it all add up to? Before addressing any of these questions directly, note several plays on the syllable y─Б╠Ж in the early part of the hymn: 1) PREV + dual rel. pronoun in the initial sequences s├бс╣Г y─Б╠Б(1c), s├бс╣Г y─Б╠Бv (our 3c) (as well as pr├б y─Б╠Б[4c] and, with slight transformation, p├бri y├бd [5c]); 2) dual verbs yam├бtuс╕е (1c), yant├бm (2c), ─Б╠Бy─Бtam (3a), yatathaс╕е (3d). These observations set the stage for a way to reason through the problems of this hemistich.

Let us begin with the problem of the lack of accented verb in what must be a rel. cl. introduced by s├бс╣Г ya├║. Assuming that d, with its unaccented verb, is the main cl. corresponding to the rel. cl. of c, which has no overt verb, there is a non-arbitrary way to generate one: in 1c the same opening sequence s├бс╣Г y─Б╠Б(differing only in the form of the dual rel. prn., attributable to the variation in the following initial) does have an accented verb, pf. yam├бtuс╕е, reinforced by the immediately flg. splv.

y├бmiс╣гс╣нh─Б, with the verb of 2c, yant├бm, also belonging to the root тИЪyam. Our opening s├бс╣Г ya├║ cries out for (or at least whispers for) a similar form of тИЪyam, and so I have supplied it. Note that the obj. of s├бm тАж yam├бtuс╕е in 1cd is j├бn─Бn as here. (Geldner [n. 3cd] supplies n├бyathaс╕е, on the basis of V.65.6 yuv├бm mitrem├бс╣Г j├бnaс╣Г, y├бtathaс╕е s├бс╣Г ca nayathaс╕е, also a M+V passage; this is a reasonable idea based on a good parallel, and in some ways amounts to the same thing: he tr. тАЬdie die Menschen zusammen(halten)тАЭ – but I prefer mine because it is generated within the hymnтАЩs context. Oldenberg appears to supply a form of тИЪyat matching the one in the main cl. of d, as does Renou) On the question of ap├бseva there is now a reasonable consensus (Oldenberg, Geldner, Renou, and me, but see Grassmann and Oldenberg for alternative views) that this represents a dual NA ap├бs─Б referring to M+V as subjects. They are therefore controlling the peoples (j├бn─Бn) as workers (or, perhaps better, work-overseers) do. But we must now confront the hapax apnasth├бс╕е. This is likely a cmpd of ├бpnas- тАШproperty, richesтАЩ and a form of тИЪsth─Б. But what form? Grassmann, Debrunner (AiG II.2.37), and EWA (s.v. ├бpnas-) assign it to a them. stem apnasth├б-, which would require it to be a nom. sg., which ill accords with the assumed dual subj. If it is nom. sg., then ap├бs─Б would be pushed into the acc. slot, where there is no syntactic place for it, or else, with an unenthusiastic suggestion of OldenbergтАЩs, it would be an instr. sg. to the neut. s-stem, for

*├бpas─Б. Better to take it, by OldenbergтАЩs preferred interpr., as belonging to a root-noun cmpd apnas-sth─Б╠Б-. Under this interpr. it would be an acc. pl. This seems the least objectionable from a contextual point of view; even though acc. pl. to root nouns in - ─Б aren’t certainly attested (see the not very helpful treatments of Lanman [Noun Inflec. 451 and passim], Macdonell VG 253), both -as and -─Бs seem to be possibilities. The 1st members of cmpds in -sth─Б╠Б- generally have a locatival relationship to their 2nd member, so тАШstanding/staying in ├бpnas-тАЩ is the likely meaning. As for its function in the clause, I take it as qualifying j├бn─Бn (so also Oldenberg, though with alternatives), while Geldner and Renou take it as part of the simile (e.g., тАЬ… die die Menschen zusammen(halten) wie Werkmeister die LohnarbeiterтАЭ), and Scarlatta, flg.

Neisser, takes it as the designation of a group of people distinct from the general j├бn─Бn but still in the frame. In the absence of other attestations of the cmpd or underlying phrase, this cannot be decisively determined. For a detailed disc. of the word and the passage, see Scarlatta 645-46.

The denom. ┼Ыrudh─лy├б- is, by most accounts (see Oldenberg, Renou), but not by GeldnerтАЩs (see n. 3d), built to the 2nd sg. impv. ┼Ыrudh├н тАШlisten!тАЩ. It is an acc. pl. part. The question is what sense it is conveying. Grassmann glosses тАШgehorsam seinтАЩ, but since even (cid) this group of people is put in its place by M+V with their greatness (mahitv─Б╠Б), it is unlikely that they were already obedient. Oldenberg (see also Renou) suggests that it is people who address M+V with this impv., perhaps indicating that they stand in a close or privileged relationship with those gods. I think rather that it may refer to people powerful enough to command obedience from other men through such peremptory commands. They would then be similar in stature to the apnasth├бс╕е: two sets of people used to getting their own way (rich and demanding), who have to submit to M+V.

Griffith

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWho (are) strong as horses, accepters or pious praise, observers of truth, whom Aditi conceived; whom, mighty of the mighty at your birth and formidable to mortal foes, she bore.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

When at her season Aditi (was ready) to bear as embryo (the two) who like prizewinning horses were of pure breed,
who were being born forth greatly great, she pushed downward (at
delivery) the two to be terrible for the cheating mortal.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The birth of M+V from Aditi. This vs. is also beset with difficulties. The major structural one is determining the interrelationships of the three subordinate clauses, in abc, marked by y─Б╠Б, y├бd, and y─Б╠Бrespectively, and their joint relationship (or not) to the main clause in d. Once again, there are numerous competing views; I will not rehearse them all. In my view, the three subordinate clauses are not all parallel and semi-independent, but rather the two introduced by the dual rel. prn. y─Б╠Б (a, c) are parallel and jointly dependent on the middle cl. introduced by y├бd (b). In tr.

I have flipped the order of a and b in hopes of making the sense a bit more parsable. I further think that the two forms of y─Б╠БтАШwhich twoтАЩ have as antecedent in b the sg.

g├бrbham: тАЬthe embryo which was those twoтАЭ or тАЬthe two as embryo.тАЭ M+V formed one of the pairs that Aditi gave birth to serially and in that sense were a single g├бrbham.

Let us then concentrate first on p─Бda a. Here, as in 1ab, there is an infin. in - dhyai predicated of a godтАЩs name, ├бditiс╕е: тАЬWhen Aditi (was) to bear.тАЭ The puzzle in the vs. is с╣Ыt─Б╠Б, and numerous analyses have been proposed: nom. sg. fem. to normally neut. с╣Ыt├б- тАШtruth (etc.)тАЩ; short instr. sg. to the same stem; dual to the same stem; a 3rd sg. denom. verb to the same stem (emending to *с╣Ыt─Бy├бd from с╣Ыt─Б╠Бy├бd), or, the solution I favor, as a short loc. sg. to с╣Ыt├║- тАШseasonтАЩ (so Geldner, though see his n. 4b), even though -u-stems supposedly have only -au/-avi locc. (but see Lanman p. 411: тАЬif there is any certain instance of a L in -├в, it must be regarded as due to false analogy.тАЭ I see no problem with analogy, false or otherwise).

The two y─Б╠Бclauses are nominal. The first (a) presents no problems. In the 2nd (c) most tr. supply a verb with pr├б, e.g., Geldner тАЬdie sich gross hervortunтАЭ (sim. Renou).

However, I take j─Б╠Бyam─Бn─Б as a predicated pres. part. and m├бhi as an intensifier of mah─Б╠Бnt─Б.

In d the sense of the verb n├н d─лdhaс╕е is unclear, and the lexeme n├н тИЪdhс╣Ы is not common. Grassmann glosses this passage as тАШmachenтАЩ with double acc.; Geldner tr. тАШhatte тАж getragenтАЩ, Renou тАШavait plac├й en secretтАЩ. In the three other passages containing n├н (─Б╠Б) тИЪdhс╣Ы that I know of (IV.2.12, VI.17.6, n├н-─Б╠БVIII.17.13), the idiom means something like тАШfixтАЩ or тАШsecureтАЩ, but here I think it applies to the process of birth: тАШbear downтАЩ.

Although I know of no other such exx., this kind of technical birth context doesn’t come up very often in the RV. The birth process interpr. fits well with the predicated pres. part. of c: тАЬwho were being bornтАЭ as well as with the indication in b that Aditi had reached her precise time for giving birth.

Griffith

Whom, of pure origin, like two strong horses, Aditi bore as babes in proper season,
Whom, Mighty at your birth, the Mighty Goddess brought forth as terrors to the mortal foeman.

Geldner

Die wie zwei siegreiche Renner von reiner Rasse, als Aditi an der Zeit war, die Leibesfrucht zu tragen, die sich gro├Я hervortun als die Gro├Яen geboren. Sie hatte die beiden als Leibesfrucht getragen, die f├╝r den heimt├╝ckischen Sterblichen furchtbar sind.

Grassmann

Die Aditi als Frucht zu tragen stark war, die rein entstammten wie zwei edle Rosse, Die kaum geboren gross gewachsen waren, die machte furchtbar sie dem b├╢sen Menschen.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬInasmuch as all the gods equally plural ased and rejoicing in your greatness conferred strength upon you, and since you are pre-eminen over the wide heaven and earth, your courses are unobstructed, unimpeded.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Your courses: spa┼Ыo adabdh─Бso am┼лr─Б: spa┼Ыaс╕е = ra┼Ыmayas c─Бra v─Б, rays, or perhaps, reins, or goings, which are ahisita, uninjured, am┼лс╕Нha, not bewildered

Jamison Brereton

Since all the gods in concert, being exhilarated, magnanimously established dominion for you two,
such that you two surround even the two wide world-halves, there exist spies (in your service), undeceivable, ungullible.

Jamison Brereton Notes

This vs. is refreshingly straightforward, even though the main cl. of d seems something of an irrelevancy after the grand statements in abc.

Griffith

As all the Gods in their great joy and gladness gave you with one accord your high dominion,
As ye surround both worlds, though wide and spacious your spies are ever true and never bewildered.

Geldner

Da alle G├╢tter euch einm├╝tig und bereitwillig frohlockend die Herrschaft bestimmten, da├Я ihr sogar die beiden weiten Welth├дlften in Obhut nehmen sollet, so stehen euch untr├╝gliche, kluge Sp├дher zu Diensten.

Grassmann

Da alle G├╢tter im Verein euch willig und hocherfreut die Herrschaft zugestanden, Da ihr umfangt die beiden weiten Welten, so sind euch Sp├дher, weise und untr├╝glich.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬYou manifest vigour daily, you strengthen the summit of the sky as if with a pillar; the solid firmamen and the universal deity (the sun) replenish earth and heaven with the food of man.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

As if with a pillar: upam─Бd iva: upam─Бt = sth┼лс╣Зa, a post or pillar– the post to which a calf is tied

Jamison Brereton

Because you uphold your dominion through the days and you make firm (heavenтАЩs) back as if from highest heaven,
firm (also) is the heavenly body [=sun], and belonging to all the gods it has stretched to earth and to heaven with the gushing [=rain] of
those two [=Mitra and Varuс╣Зa].

Jamison Brereton Notes

The vs. is knit together with phonological and etymological figures. Each p─Бda contains a form of div/dyu: a dy┼л╠Бn, b dyoс╕е, c -devo, d dy─Б╠Бm. Note also the phonological similarity of the two du. verbs dh─Бr├бyethe (a), dс╣Ыс╣Гh├йthe (b), with the latter reprised etymologically by dс╣Ыс╕╖h├│ in c. P─Бdas b and d also rhyme.

Unlike the standard tr. I take b as part of the h├н cl. beginning in a, with cd as the main cl. Since the verb of b, dс╣Ыс╣Гh├йthe, is initial, it can owe its accent either to its position (as most interpr. it) or to belonging to a subord. cl., as I do. Nonetheless, there is little riding on this choice, though I would support mine by pointing out that the fact that M+V made the back of heaven firm (b) could serve as a reason why the sun is also firmly fixed (c).

Contra Klein (explicitly, DGRV I.379-80) and Geldner/Renou (implicitly), I do not think that ut├б, positioned in the middle of c, conjoins b and c, but instead begins a new cl., which continues through d.

With Geldner (and, judging from his tr., Renou), I divide dh─Бs├нn─Бy├│с╕е into dh─Бs├нn─Б ay├│с╕е, with the gen.-loc. du. of ay├бm, not ─Бy├│с╕е, gen.-abl. sg. of ─Бy├║- with the Pp.

Griffith

So, through the days maintaining princely power. ye prop the height as ’twere from loftiest heaven.
The Star of all the Gods, established, filleth the heaven and earth with food of man who liveth.

Geldner

Denn ihr behauptet eure Herrschaft Tag f├╝r Tag; ihr festigt die H├╢he des Himmels gleichsam vom h├╢chsten Himmel aus. Und das gefestete Gestirn, das allen G├╢ttern geh├╢rt, hat Erde und Himmel mit dem Labsal beider bezogen.

Grassmann

Denn ihr behauptet fort und fort die Herrschaft, des Himmels Kuppe st├╝tzt ihr wie zwei Pfeiler; Der feste Sterngott und der Allgott spannte zum Sitz der Wesen Erde aus und Himmel.

Elizarenkova

рддрд╛ рддреМ рдорд┐рддреНрд░рд╛рд╡рд░реБрдгреМ рдпреБрд╡рд╛рдВ рд╡рд┐рдЧреНрд░рдВ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдЬреНрдЮрдВ рдпрдЬрдорд╛рдирдореН ред тАШрд╡рд┐рдкреНрд░рдГ рд╡рд┐рдЧреНрд░рдГ’ рдЗрддрд┐ рдореЗрдзрд╛рд╡рд┐рдирд╛рдорд╕реБ рдкрд╛рдард╛рддреН ред рдзреИрдереЗ рдзрд╛рд░рдпрдердГ рдЬрдард░рдореН рдЙрджрд░рдВ рдкреГрдгрдзреНрдпреИ рд╕реЛрдореЗрди рдкреВрд░рдпрд┐рддреБрдореН ред рдпрддреН рдпрджрд╛ рд╕рднреГрддрдпрдГ рд╕рд╣ рднреНрд░рд┐рдпрдорд╛рдгрд╛ рдЛрддреНрд╡рд┐рдЬрдГ рд╕рджреНрдо рдпрдЬреНрдЮрд╕рджрдирдореН рдЖ рдкреГрдгрдиреНрддрд┐ рдЖрдкреВрд░рдпрдиреНрддрд┐ ред рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рдЬрд┐рдиреНрд╡рд╛ рд╣реЗ рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рдЬрд┐рдиреНрд╡рд╛рдиреМ рдпрддреН рдпрджрд╛ рдкрдпрдГ рдЬрд▓рдВ рднрд╡рджреНрднреНрдпрд╛рдВ рдкреНрд░рд╣рд┐рддрдВ рддрджрд╛ рдпреБрд╡рддрдпрдГ рдирджреНрдпрдГ рджрд┐рд╢реЛ рд╡рд╛ рди рдореГрд╖реНрдпрдиреНрддреЗ рд░рдЬрд╕рд╛ рдирд╛рднрд┐рднреВрдпрдиреНрддреЗ ред рдЕрд╡рд╛рддрд╛рдГ рдЕрд╢реБрд╖реНрдХрд╛рд╢реНрдЪ рд╡рд┐ рднрд░рдиреНрддреЗ рд╡рд┐рднреВрддрд┐рдВ рдзрд╛рд░рдпрдиреНрддрд┐ рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬYou two support the sage (worshipper), filling his belly when he and his dependants fill the sacrificial chamber; when sustainers of all, the rain (is sent down by you), and the young (rivers) are not obstructed, but, undried, diffuse (fertility) around.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

You should appropriate the lively (soma) to fill your belly, when those of the same pedigree [=soma-pressing fingers?] fill the seat.
The unsurpassable maidens [=fingers] are not neglectful when they
distribute their milk [=soma], o you two who enliven all.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Geldner follows S─Бyaс╣Зa. in interpr. this vs. as referring to rain and river waters.

Although this would accord better with the enigmatic gush (dh─Бs├н-) of 6d, it doesnтАЩt fit the vocabulary or apparent sense of this enigmatic vs. The best clue we have is p─Бda a, where тАЬto fill the bellyтАЭ (jaс╣нh├бram pс╣Ыс╣З├бdhyai) belongs to a phrase for drinking soma to satiation (cf. nearby VI.69.7 and V.34.2, X.104.2, as well as other locutions involving soma and the belly). (Both Oldenberg and Renou also take the p─Бda as referring to soma.) Once the poet has established the soma context with this reasonably clear phraseology, he can (and does) treat the subject in a more obscure fashion.

In b and c I take the feminine plurals s├бbhс╣Ыtayaс╕е тАШof the same rearing / pedigreeтАЩ and yuvat├бy├▓ тАЩv─Бt─Бс╕е тАШunsurpassable maidensтАЩ as referring to the fingers (of the priests) that press the soma. Such locutions, referring to the shared kinship of the fingers (because they belong to the same hand), are frequent in the IXth Maс╣Зс╕Нala and the forms are always feminine. I am tolerably certain of the second identification, since the action ascribed to them in p─Бda d, distributing their тАЬmilk,тАЭ would be a reasonable way (given the tropes of soma preparation) to characterize the work of the pressing fingers. I am less certain about the identification in b, because тАЬfill the seatтАЭ (s├бdma тАж pс╣Ыс╣З├бnti) is not as easy to connect with soma preparation. тАЬSeatтАЭ could refer, inter alia, to the ritual ground or the cosmos – both are attested – but neither is generally flooded with soma. s├бbhс╣Ыti- is a hapax, so it does not help identify the referent. So the sense of p─Бda b remains in doubt for me.

Note another ex. of a -dhyai infinitive, though this time not as the predicated substitute for a main verb.

Griffith

Take the strong drink, to quaff till ye are sated, when he and his attendants fill the chamber.
The young Maids brook not that none seeks to win them, when, Quickeners of all! they scatter moisture.

Geldner

Ihr sollet Eile machen den Leib zu f├╝llen, wenn sie bei gleicher Pflege ihren Stand ausf├╝llen. Nicht vergessen es die un├╝bertroffenen Jungfrauen, ihr Allbeleber, wenn sie ihre Milch verteilen.

Grassmann

So nehmt den starken Trank, den Bauch zu f├╝llen, wenn euren Sitz die Speisebringer f├╝llen; Es s├дumen nicht die unverletzten Jungfrau’n, wenn Milch sie euch, o Allbeleber, bringen.

Elizarenkova

рддрд╛ рддреМ рдорд┐рддреНрд░рд╛рд╡рд░реБрдгреМ рдпреБрд╡рд╛рдВ рд╕реБрдореЗрдзрд╛рдГ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдЬреНрдЮрдГ рдЬрд┐рд╣реНрд╡рдпрд╛ рд╡рд╛рдЪрд╛ рд╕рджрдВ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рджрд╛ рдЗрджрдВ рдЬрд▓рдореН рдЖ рдпрд╛рдЪрддреЗ ред рдЖ рдЗрддреНрдпреБрдкрд╕рд░реНрдЧрджрд░реНрд╢рдирд╛рддреН рдпреЛрдЧреНрдпрдХреНрд░рд┐рдпрд╛рдзреНрдпрд╛рд╣рд╛рд░рд╛рдд рдпрд╛рдЪрдд рдЗрддреНрдпрдзреНрдпрд╛рд╣реНрд░рд┐рдпрддреЗ ред рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╕реНрдпрд╛рдореГрдЪрд┐ рдЬрд▓рд╕реНрдп рдкреНрд░рдХреГрддрддреНрд╡рд╛рддреН рдмреБрджреНрдзреМ рд╡рд┐рдкрд░рд┐рд╡рд░реНрддрдорд╛рдирдВ рдЬрд▓рдорд┐рджрдВрд╢рдмреНрджреЗрди рдкрд░рд╛рдореГрд╢реНрдпрддреЗ ред рдпрддреН рдпрджрд╛ рд╡рд╛рдВ рдпреБрд╡рдпреЛрдГ рдЕрд░рддрд┐рдГ рдЕрднрд┐рдЧрдиреНрддрд╛ рдЛрддреЗ рдпрдЬреНрдЮреЗ рд╕рддреНрдпрдГ рдорд╛рдпрд╛рд░рд╣рд┐рддрдГ рдЖ рднреВрддреН рдЖрднрд╡рддрд┐ рд╣реЗ рдШреГрддрд╛рдиреНрдиреМ рддрддреН рдорд╣рд┐рддреНрд╡рдореН рдЕрдкреЗрдХреНрд╖рд┐рддрдкреНрд░рджрд╛рддреГрддреНрд╡рд▓рдХреНрд╖рдгрдВ рд╡рд╛рдВ рдпреБрд╡рдпреЛрдГ рдЕрд╕реНрддреБ ред рдХрд┐рдВрдЪ рдпреБрд╡рдВ рдпреБрд╡рд╛рдВ рджрд╛рд╢реБрд╖реЗ рджрд╛рд╢реБрд╖реЛ рдпрдЬрдорд╛рдирд╕реНрдп рее рд╖рд╖реНрдареНрдпрд░реНрдереЗ рдЪрддреБрд░реНрдереА рее рдЕрдВрд╣рдГ рдкрд╛рдкрдВ рд╡рд┐ рдЪрдпрд┐рд╖реНрдЯрдВ рд╡рд┐рдирд╛рд╢рдпрддрдорд┐рддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe wise man always (solicits) you his prayers for this (supply of water), when approaching you sincer in sacrifice; may your magnanimity be such that you, the feeders upon gh─л, may exterminate sin in the donor (of the oblation);тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

With his prayers: with his tongue, jihvay─Б

Jamison Brereton

(You) two (does) the one of good wisdom [=Agni] always (call) here with his tongue, when the true wheel (of the sacrifice) [=Agni] has
come to be without you.
Let this be your greatness, you who have ghee for food: you open up the narrow place for the pious one.

Jamison Brereton Notes

P─Бda a lacks a verb; on its structure and on the grammatical interpr. of sumedh─Б╠Б(с╕е), see esp. Oldenberg Since it is likely that sumedh─Б╠Б(с╕е) is a nom. sg., referring to Agni, this slots the du. t─Б╠Бinto the acc., and we need a verb to link the two. Though OldenbergтАЩs тАШleadтАЩ is possible, I follow Geldner(/Renou) in supplying тАШcallтАЩ, since this connects this ritual vs. with those in the earlier parts of the hymn (2ab, 3ab; see published introduction. and comm. ad locc.). As is generally recognized, the referent of the nom. is Agni; III.57.5, adduced by Oldenberg, makes this quite clear: y─Б╠Бte jihv─Б╠Бmadhumat─л╠Бsumedh─Б╠Б, ├бgne тАж The word arat├н- тАШspoked wheelтАЩ in b is another word regularly applied to Agni.

This p─Бda also contains, by most interpr., two words associated with truth, saty├б-, modifying arat├н-, and с╣Ыt├б-, but these interpr. are hard-pressed to come up with a convincing interpr. of the loc. с╣Ыt├й. By contrast, I interpr. it as I do the similarly structured II.29.4 m─Б╠Бvo r├бthaс╕е тАж с╣Ыt├й bh┼лt, where, with Renou, I take с╣Ыt├й as the postposition тАШwithoutтАЩ, construed with a pronominal enclitic in 2nd position: тАЬLet (our) chariot not come to be without you.тАЭ See comm. ad loc. In the passage here I assume that the absence of M+V at the ritual ground induces Agni to call them with his tongue (=crackling). This interpr. also fits with the rivalry vss. to follow (9-11): if M+V are not here, where are they? Probably at the sacrifice of a competitor. In the comm. to II.29.4 I consider an alternative interpr. with с╣Ыt├й the loc. of с╣Ыt├б- тАШtruthтАЩ. If I were to do so here, the passage could mean тАЬwhen the spoked wheel (of the sacrifice) [=Agni] has come into existence / has been realized for you at/in the truth [=the sacrifice or place of sacrifice?].тАЭ I still prefer the published solution.

On (vi) cayiс╣гс╣нam see Hoffmann, Aufs. II.367.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬ(Exterminate also), Mitra and Varuс╣Зa those who emulously contending, disturb the rites that are agreeable and beneficial to you both; those divinities, those mortals, who are not diligent in adoration, those who performing works perform not sacrifices, those who do not propitiate you.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Exterminate also: na ye dev─Бsa ohas─Б na mart─Б ayaj├▒as─Бco apyo na putr─Бс╕е: ohas─Б = vahanas─Бdhanena, by the means of conveying– perhaps wishes, i.e. stotreс╣Зa, by praise;

Apyaс╕е = karmavantaс╕е, doing acts, from apas, but not sacrificin o sacrificing in vain, vс╣Ыth─Б karm─Бс╣Зi kurvantaс╕е; na putr─БH = not sons, apс╣Ыс╣Зantaс╕е, not plural asing, or satisfying

Jamison Brereton

When they start contending over you two but violate the dear
ordinances ordained by you, Mitra and Varuс╣Зa,
they, not attending upon the sacrifice, are neither gods, despite their
vaunting, nor mortals, but like children who do not swell [=grow/thrive].

Jamison Brereton Notes

The first half of this vs. is fairly straightforward; the problems arise in the 2nd hemistich, primarily because of ├бpi yaс╕е in d. The first hemistich describes the behavior of the contentious and impious rivals, while the 2nd defines such people as outside the normal categories of beings. P─Бda c asserts clearly that those who donтАЩt attend upon the sacrifice are neither gods nor men, and in d they are compared instead to ├бpi yaс╕е тАж putr─Б╠Бс╕е, which is universally tr. as тАЬlike the sons of the watery femaleтАЭ (e.g., Geldner тАЬwie die S├╢hne der WasserfrauтАЭ). Not only does this make no obvious (or unobvious) sense, but the morphology is essentially impossible: it is very difficult to get ├бpi yaс╕е to be either the gen. sg. of a fem. -─л-stem or the nom. pl. m. of an adj. See the rather despairing assessments of Geldner (n. 9d), Debrunner (AiG II.2.401), and esp. Scarlatta (592 n. 841). Desperate situations require desperate measures, and I therefore part company with the consensus interpr. of ├бpi yaс╕е and suggest an entirely different derivation – as a negated root noun cmpd to the seс╣н form of the тАШswellтАЩ root тИЪp─л. We should expect a root-accented *a-p─л╠Б-, with nom. pl.

*ap├нyaс╕е, but I would suggest that this unclear hapax would have been attracted to the reasonably well-attested тАШwateryтАЩ stem ├бpi ya- and the accent retracted. As for meaning, I suggest that тАШnot swelling/swollenтАЩ means тАШnot growing / thrivingтАЩ, and in reference to children to stunted or underdeveloped ones, afflicted by what is now called тАЬfailure to thriveтАЭ in pediatric medicine. I do not know an easy way to do this, but might suggest an alternative tr. of cd as тАЬthose not attending on the sacrifice who are neither gods тАж nor mortals are like children тАжтАЭ

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWhen the intelligent (priests) offer praise, then some of them, glorifying (Agni and other deities), recite the Nivid hymns; such being the case, we address to you sincere adoration, for in consequence of your greatness you do not associate with (other) divinities.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Na kir devebhir yatathaс╕е, you do not go, gacchathaс╕е, with other gods, anyair devaiс╕е saha, you are not associated with them at sacrifice

Jamison Brereton

When the praisers distribute their speech and some recite the formal invocations, paying them heed,
after that we will speak to you pronouncements that come true: тАЬNo one (will violate your ordinances). You set in their places (the
peoples) along with the gods by your greatness.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton Notes

Geldner and Renou take the first hemistich here as a continuation of the description of bad ritual behavior, with cd introducing our contrastively correct practice. I think rather that the whole of 10 describes this good behavior. One advantage of this interpr. is that it allows ─Б╠Бd opening c to have its normal sense тАШafter thatтАЩ, which Klein (DGRV II.135-36) must explicitly deny it. By my interpr. the first p─Бda sets the ritual scene, with the various priestly speakers тАЬdistributingтАЭ the types of ritual speech, as is standard in Vedic ritual. Some of these speakers recite the Nivids, the formal invocations. After this тАЬweтАЭ take over by speaking ukth├б-.

On k─лst├б- тАШpraiserтАЩ see comm. ad I.127.7. I see no evidence for RenouтАЩs тАШmauvaispr├кtresтАЩ beyond his contextual assumptions.

The interpr. of ab as referring to bad practice turns on the part. man─Бn─Б╠Бс╕е, which most take as meaning тАШ(falsely) considering X as YтАЩ (e.g., Geldner тАЬwas sie f├╝r Einladungsspr├╝che haltenтАЭ), but no evidence is presented that this should be the meaning of this root aor. part., the only occurrence of the participial stem. Most other forms of this medial root aor. (mostly attested in the subjunctive) have a positive sense: тАШbring to mindтАЩ, тАШconceiveтАЩ, тАШponderтАЩ, etc. The published translation has тАШpay heed toтАЩ, but any of the other suggested tr. just given would work as well, while тАШ(falsely) considerтАЩ has no support in this stem.

P─Бda d is syntactically problematic. The last two words (yatatho mahitv─Б╠Б) are identical to the ending of 3d and appear to sketch a ring and a return to the focus on M+VтАЩs ability to put human beings in order. Because of this salient repetition, I am reluctant to ascribe an entire different sense to this phrase in this vs. than in 3, as both Geldner and Renou do, with both also unacceptably stretching the meaning of the verb form. In order to take d as a single cl., they must also treat n├бkiс╕е as a simple neg.

rather than in its usual meaning тАШno oneтАЩ, since the verb yatathaс╕е is 2nd du. and cannot take тАШno oneтАЩ as subject. In order to avoid this problem, I create problems of my own. I take n├бkiс╕е as a radically truncated sentence тАЬNo one тАжтАЭ This is based on the observation that one of the most common contexts in which n├бkis appears is as subj. of minat (etc.) тАШviolate(s)тАЩ (cf., e.g., I.69.7, IV.30.23, VI.30.2, etc.). I therefore suggest that n├бkiс╕е here is an implicit response to the description of the behavior of bad rivals in 9b priy─Б╠Бdh─Б╠Бma yuv├бdhit─Б min├бnti тАЬthey violate the dear ordinances ordained by youтАЭ. Here in our ritual тАЬno oneтАЭ performs such violation. With n├бkis out of the way, the rest of the p─Бda can be harmonized with the use of yatatho mahitv─Б╠Бin 3d. There M+V тАШset in placeтАЩ various peoples (j├бn─Бn). Here I would resupply j├бn─Бn and take dev├йbhiс╕е as an instr. of accompaniment: M+V set in place the peoples along with the gods. I would prefer not to have to impose such a radical analysis on this p─Бda, but I find other analyses even more unsatisfactory.

рд╣реЗ рдорд┐рддреНрд░рд╛рд╡рд░реБрдгреМ рдЕрд╡реЛрдГ рдЕрд╡рддреЛрдГ рд╡рд╛рдВ рдпреБрд╡рдпреЛрдГ рдЕрднрд┐рд╖реНрдЯреМ рдЕрднрд┐рдЧрдордиреЗ рдЫрд░реНрджрд┐рд╖рдГ рдЧреГрд╣рд╛рдп рд╕реБрдЦрд╛рде рд╡рд╛ ред рдЪрддреБрд░реНрдереНрдпрд░реНрдереЗ рд╖рд╖реНрдареА ред рдпреБрд╡рд╛рдорднрд┐рдЧрддреЗрд╖реБ рд╕реНрддреЛрддреГрд╖реБ рдпреБрд╡реЛрдГ рдпреБрд╡рдпреЛрдГ рд╕рдВрдмрдиреНрдзрд┐ рдпреБрд╡рд╛рднреНрдпрд╛рдВ рджреЗрдпрдВ рддрджреНрдЧреГрд╣рд╛рджрд┐рдХрдореН рдЕрд╕реНрдХреГрдзреЛрдпреБ рдЕрд╡рд┐рдЪреНрдЫрд┐рдиреНрдирдВ рднрд╡рддрд┐ ред рддрдерд╛ рдЪ рдпрд╛рд╕реНрдХрдГ- тАШ рдЕрд╕реНрдХреГрдзреЛрдпреБрд░рдХреГрдзреНрд╡рд╛рдпреБрдГ ред рдХреГрдзреНрд╡рд┐рддрд┐ рд╣реНрд░рд╕реНрд╡рдирд╛рдо рдирд┐рдХреГрддреНрддрдВ рднрд╡рддрд┐ ’ (рдирд┐рд░реБ. рем. рей ) рдЗрддрд┐ ред рдЗрддреНрдерд╛ рд╕рддреНрдпрдореЗрд╡ ред рдХрджрд╛ рдорд┐рддреНрд░рд╛рд╡рд░реБрдгрдпреЛрд░рднрд┐рдЧрдордирдорд┐рддреНрдпрдд рдЖрд╣ ред рдпрддреН рдпрджрд╛ рдЧрд╛рд╡рдГ рд╕реНрддреБрддрдпрдГ рдЕрдиреБ рд╕реНрдлреБрд░рд╛рдиреН рдЕрдиреБрд╕реНрдлреБрд░реЗрдпреБрдГред рдпрджрд╛ рдЪ рдЛрдЬрд┐рдкреНрдпрдореН рдЛрдЬреБрдЧрд╛рдорд┐рдирдВ рдзреГрд╖реНрдгреБрдВ рд╢рддреНрд░реВрдгрд╛рдВ рдзрд░реНрд╖рдХрдВ рд╡реГрд╖рдгрдВ рдХрд╛рдорд╛рдирд╛рдВ рд╡рд░реНрд╖рд┐рддрд╛рд░рдВ рд╕реЛрдордВ рд░рдгреЗ рд░рдордгреЗ рдпрдЬреНрдЮреЗ рдпреБрдирдЬрдиреН рдпрдЬрдорд╛рдирд╛ рдпреБрдЮреНрдЬреНрдпреБрдГ рее рее резреж рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬUpon your approach, Mitra and Varuс╣Зa, protectors of the dwelling, your (bounty) is unlimited; when (your) praises are uttered, and the sacrificers add in the ceremony the Soma that inspires straightforwardness and resoluion, and is the showerer (of benefits).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Your bounty: yuvor askс╣Ыdhoyu: yuv─Бbhy─Бm deyam gс╣Ыh─Бdikam avicchinnam bhavati, that which is to be given by you, as houses and the like, is unchecked;

Askс╣Ыdhoyu = long-lived, akс╣Ыdhv─Бyuс╕е kс╣Ыdhu meaning short, or nikс╣Ыttam, cut off; there is also association with ajara as in: yo askс╣Ыdhoyur ajaraс╕е svarv─Бn, who is long-lived, free from decay, an occupant of heaven (askс╣Ыdhoyurakс╣Ыdhv─Бyuс╕е kс╣Ыdhviti hasvan─Бma nikс╣Ыttam bhavati: Nirukta 6.3)

Jamison Brereton

In just this way, in the charge of you two and of your shelter, (we seek) of you, Mitra and Varuс╣Зa, (giving) that is not stunted,
when the cows [=milk mixture] will bound after the straight-flying one [=soma], when they will yoke the bold bull [=soma] in battle-lust.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The first hemistich lacks a verb, but something like тАШwe seekтАЩ is a reasonable bet, to govern ├бskс╣Ыdhoyu тАШnot stuntedтАЩ, which elsewhere modifies тАШwealthтАЩ (VI.22.3) and тАШtreasure-conferralтАЩ (VII.53.3), hence my тАШgivingтАЩ.

Geldner produces an elaborate interpr. of cd as a portrayal of battle: тАШcowsтАЩ = bow string, тАШstraight-flying oneтАЩ = arrow. Although such tropes would be at home in other parts of the RV, I see no martial context in this hymn that would encourage such a reading. Better to interpr. the hemistich within a ritual context, since this has been prominent in the hymn. The cows can, as so often, be the milk meant to be mixed with the soma; the тАШstraight-flying oneтАЩ (с╣Ыjipy├б-, on which see comm. ad IV.27.4) can be the soma, or, as in IV.27.4, the falcon that carried the soma, and the bull in d is also the soma. Renou follows GeldnerтАЩs battle interpr., though (in his comm.) he also sees it overlaid with soma imagery.

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдЕрд╡реЛрдГ) рд░рдХреНрд╖рдХрдпреЛрдГред рдЕрддреНрд░ рдЫрд╛рдиреНрджрд╕реЛ рд╡рд░реНрдгрд▓реЛрдкреЛ рд╡реЗрддрд┐ рд╕рд▓реЛрдкрдГред (рдЗрддреНрдерд╛) рдЕрд╕реНрдорд╛рджреНрдзреЗрддреЛрдГ (рд╡рд╛рдореН) рдпреБрд╡рдпреЛ (рдЫрд░реНрджрд┐рд╖рдГ) рдЧреГрд╣рд╕реНрдп (рдЕрднрд┐рд╖реНрдЯреМ) рдЖрднрд┐рдореБрдЦреНрдпреЗрди рдпрдЬрдирдХреНрд░рд┐рдпрд╛рдпрд╛рдореН (рдпреБрд╡реЛрдГ) рдпреБрд╡рдпреЛрдГ (рдорд┐рддреНрд░рд╛рд╡рд░реБрдгреМ) рд╡рд╛рдпреБрд╕реВрд░реНрдпрд╡рджреНрд╡рд░реНрддреНрддрдорд╛рдиреМ (рдЕрд╕реНрдХреГрдзреЛрдпреБ) рдп рдЖрддреНрдордирдГ рдХреГрдзреБ рд╣реНрд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреНрд╡рдВ рдиреЗрдЪреНрдЫрддрд┐ред рдЕрддреНрд░ рд╕реБрдкрд╛рдВ рд╕реБрд▓реБрдЧрд┐рддрд┐ рд╕реБрд▓реЛрдкрдГред (рдЕрдиреБ) (рдпрддреН) рдпреЗ (рдЧрд╛рд╡рдГ) рдХрд┐рд░рдгрд╛ рдзреЗрдирд╡реЛ рд╡рд╛ (рд╕реНрдлреБрд░рд╛рдиреН) рд╕реНрдлреВрд░реНрддреНрддрд┐рдорддрдГ (рдЛрдЬрд┐рдкреНрдпрдореН) рдЛрдЬреВрдирд╛рдВ рдкрд╛рд▓рдХреЗ рднрд╡рдореН (рдзреГрд╖реНрдгреБрдореН) рджреГрдврдВ рдкреНрд░рдЧрд▓реНрднрдВ рд╡рд╛ (рдпрддреН) рдпрдГ (рд░рдгреЗ) рд╕рдЩреНрдЧреНрд░рд╛рдореЗ (рд╡реГрд╖рдгрдореН) рдмрд▓рд┐рд╖реНрдардореН (рдпреБрдирдЬрддреН) рдпреБрдЮреНрдЬрдиреН реерезрезрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рд╣реЗ рдЕрдзреНрдпрд╛рдкрдХреЛрдкрджреЗрд╢рдХрд╛ рдпреЗ рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рд░реНрдерд┐рдиреЛ рдпреБрд╖реНрдорд╛рдХрдВ рдХрд╛рд░реНрдпреНрдпрдВ рд╕реНрд╡рдХрд╛рд░реНрдпреНрдпрд╡рдЬреНрдЬрд╛рдирдиреНрддрд┐ рдд рдПрд╡ рджреАрд░реНрдШрд╛рдпреБрд╖рдГ рдкреНрд░рд╢рд╕реНрддрд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛ рдзрд╛рд░реНрдорд┐рдХрд╛рдГ рдкрд░реЛрдкрдХрд╛рд░рд┐рдгреЛ рдЬрд╛рдпрдиреНрдд рдЗрддрд┐ реерезрезрее рдЕрддреНрд░ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдгреЛрджрд╛рдирд╡рджрдзреНрдпрд╛рдкрдХреЛрдкрджреЗрд╢рдХрдЧреБрдгрд╡рд░реНрдгрдирд╛рджреЗрддрджрд░реНрдерд╕реНрдп рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╛рд░реНрдереЗрди рд╕рд╣ рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрддрд┐рд░реНрд╡реЗрджреНрдпрд╛ рее рдЗрддрд┐ рд╕рдкреНрддрд╖рд╖реНрдЯрд┐рддрдордВ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдВ рджрд╢рдореЛ рд╡рд░реНрдЧрд╢реНрдЪ рд╕рдорд╛рдкреНрддрдГ рее

рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрд╛ рдЬреЛрд╢реА тЖР рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рдо) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рд╣реЗ рдЕрдзреНрдпрд╛рдкрдХ, рдЙрдкрджреЗрд╢рдХрд╛рдВрдиреЛ ! рдЬреЗ рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рд░реНрдереА рддреБрдордЪреНрдпрд╛ рдХрд╛рд░реНрдпрд╛рд▓рд╛ рдЖрдкрд▓реЗ рдХрд╛рд░реНрдп рдорд╛рдирддрд╛рдд рддреЗрдЪ рджреАрд░реНрдШрд╛рдпреБ рдкреНрд░рд╢рдВрд╕рд┐рдд, рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рдпреБрдХреНрдд, рдзрд╛рд░реНрдорд┐рдХ рд╡ рдкрд░реЛрдкрдХрд╛рд░реА рдЕрд╕рддрд╛рдд. рее резрез рее
